[Applyconfigurations: The Typed Client API](#7-applyconfigurations-the-typed-client-api)\n8. [Extension Points and Customization Hooks](#8-extension-points-and-customization-hooks)\n9. [Operational Implications](#9-operational-implications)\n10. [Failure Modes and Design Tradeoffs](#10-failure-modes-and-design-tradeoffs)\n11. [File and Directory Map](#11-file-and-directory-map)\n\n---\n\n## 1. Subsystem Purpose and Boundaries\n\nServer-Side Apply (SSA) is the Kubernetes mechanism that moves intent reconciliation from the client to the API server. Where traditional `kubectl apply` computed a three-way merge locally (comparing the `kubectl.kubernetes.io/last-applied-configuration` annotation against the live object and the local manifest), SSA performs the merge on the server and maintains a persistent, per-field ownership record stored directly in `metadata.managedFields` on every API object.\n\nThe goals of SSA are:\n\n- **Intent preservation across multiple actors.** Multiple controllers or human operators can each own disjoint subsets of fields on the same object. One actor setting a label cannot accidentally delete another actor's annotation.\n- **Conflict detection.** If actor B tries to change a field already owned by actor A, the server returns HTTP 409 with a structured conflict error rather than silently clobbering A's intent.\n- **Idempotent ownership tracking.** Applying the exact same configuration twice produces the same object and managedFields, making it safe to use from reconciliation loops.\n\n### Boundaries\n\nSSA operates entirely within the API server's PATCH endpoint for content-type `application/apply-patch+yaml` (or `application/apply-patch+cbor` behind a feature gate). It is not a separate service. Its upstream dependency is the `structured-merge-diff` library (`sigs.k8s.io/structured-merge-diff/v6`) which supplies the actual field-level merge and conflict algorithm. Its downstream dependency is the etcd storage layer, reached through the `rest.Patcher` interface.\n\nSSA does **not** govern watch, list, get, or delete. It interacts with the admission chain (mutating and validating webhooks), but only as a caller — SSA itself is not a webhook.\n\n---\n\n## 2. Key Components and Responsibility Split\n\n### 2.1 `FieldManager` (public facade)\n\n**Package:** `k8s.io/apimachinery/pkg/util/managedfields`\n**Files:** `fieldmanager.go`, `extract.go`, `scalehandler.go`, `gvkparser.go`, `typeconverter.go`\n\n`FieldManager` is the public interface exposed to apiserver handler code. It has two methods:\n\n- `Apply(liveObj, appliedObj runtime.Object, manager string, force bool)` — used for SSA requests.\n- `Update(liveObj, newObj runtime.Object, manager string)` — used for ordinary PUT/PATCH requests to keep managedFields in sync without conflict checks.\n- `UpdateNoErrors(...)` — a non-fatal version of `Update` used by legacy patch paths where managedFields bookkeeping is best-effort.\n\n`FieldManager` is a type alias for `internal.FieldManager`:\n\n```go\n// staging/src/k8s.io/apimachinery/pkg/util/managedfields/fieldmanager.go:32\ntype FieldManager = internal.FieldManager\n```\n\nConstruction is done through two public constructors:\n\n- `NewDefaultFieldManager` — for built-in types backed by OpenAPI schemas.\n- `NewDefaultCRDFieldManager` — for CRDs; uses a deduced type converter that treats every field as atomic, enabling SSA for schemas that may not be fully defined.\n\nBoth constructors call `internal.NewDefaultFieldManager`, which assembles the decorator chain described in section 4.\n\n### 2.2 `internal.Manager` interface\n\n**Package:** `k8s.io/apimachinery/pkg/util/managedfields/internal`\n**File:** `manager.go`\n\n```\ntype Manager interface {\n    Update(liveObj, newObj runtime.Object, managed Managed, manager string) (runtime.Object, Managed, error)\n    Apply(liveObj, appliedObj runtime.Object, managed Managed, manager string, force bool) (runtime.Object, Managed, error)\n}\n```\n\nEvery decorator layer in the chain implements this interface. The chain is assembled at startup and is immutable for the lifetime of the API server process.\n\n### 2.3 `structuredMergeManager`\n\n**File:** `staging/src/k8s.io/apimachinery/pkg/util/managedfields/internal/structuredmerge.go`\n\nThis is the innermost (leaf) implementation. It holds a `merge.Updater` from `sigs.k8s.io/structured-merge-diff`, a `TypeConverter` that bridges Kubernetes `runtime.Object` to SMD `typed.TypedValue`, and a `versionConverter` that lets SMD convert objects between API versions when evaluating field ownership across version boundaries.\n\nFor `Apply`, it:\n1. Validates that the patch object carries the same GV as the resource's current version.\n2. Rejects any patch that carries `managedFields` (forbidden in apply patches).\n3. Converts both live and patch objects to `typed.TypedValue` via the `TypeConverter`.\n4. Calls `f.updater.Apply(...)` which runs the SMD merge algorithm.\n5. Converts the resulting typed value back to a `runtime.Object`, applies defaults, then converts to the internal hub version.\n\nFor `Update`, it calls `f.updater.Update(...)` without conflict detection.\n\n### 2.4 `TypeConverter`\n\n**File:** `staging/src/k8s.io/apimachinery/pkg/util/managedfields/internal/typeconverter.go`\n\nConverts between `runtime.Object` and `typed.TypedValue`. Two implementations:\n\n- `typeConverter` — backed by the OpenAPI v3 schema parsed at server startup. Each GVK maps to an SMD schema type, enabling per-field type awareness during merging.\n- `deducedTypeConverter` — used for CRDs without a full schema. All fields are treated as atomic scalars, which is safe but prevents granular field ownership.\n\n`NewTypeConverter` is fed OpenAPI schema maps (from `k8s.io/kube-openapi`), which are converted by `schemaconv.ToSchemaFromOpenAPI` into SMD schema types.\n\n### 2.5 `GvkParser`\n\n**File:** `staging/src/k8s.io/apimachinery/pkg/util/managedfields/gvkparser.go`\n\nWraps the SMD `typed.Parser` to enable GVK-based schema lookup. Built from `proto.Models` (the aggregated OpenAPI Protobuf model), it maps each GVK to the schema type name used by the SMD parser. This is the bridge from `k8s.io/kube-openapi` to `sigs.k8s.io/structured-merge-diff`.\n\n### 2.6 HTTP Handler (`patch.go`)\n\n**File:** `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/endpoints/handlers/patch.go`\n\n`PatchResource` is the HTTP handler factory for the PATCH endpoint. It reads the `Content-Type` header to determine the patch type, then instantiates one of three mechanism types:\n\n| Patch type | Content-Type | Mechanism |\n|---|---|---|\n| JSON Patch | `application/json-patch+json` | `jsonPatcher` |\n| Merge Patch | `application/merge-patch+json` | `jsonPatcher` |\n| Strategic Merge | `application/strategic-merge-patch+json` | `smpPatcher` |\n| **Server-Side Apply** | `application/apply-patch+yaml` | `applyPatcher` |\n| SSA (CBOR) | `application/apply-patch+cbor` | `applyPatcher` |\n\nFor SSA, `applyPatcher.applyPatchToCurrentObject` calls `p.fieldManager.Apply(...)`:\n\n```go\n// staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/endpoints/handlers/patch.go:514\nobj, err := p.fieldManager.Apply(obj, patchObj, p.options.FieldManager, force)\n```\n\nThe `force` flag is derived from `PatchOptions.Force`. When `true`, the applying manager takes ownership of any conflicting fields, resolving the conflict by displacing the previous owner.\n\n### 2.7 Admission Guard (`fieldmanager/admission.go`)\n\n**File:** `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/endpoints/handlers/fieldmanager/admission.go`\n\n`NewManagedFieldsValidatingAdmissionController` wraps the existing admission chain. After mutating webhooks run, it validates that the `managedFields` they left behind are still well-formed. If a webhook corrupted `managedFields` (e.g., an outdated webhook that blindly copies the object), the guard reverts `managedFields` to their pre-admission state and emits a warning rather than returning a 500:\n\n```go\n// staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/endpoints/handlers/fieldmanager/admission.go:74\nif err := managedfields.ValidateManagedFields(managedFieldsAfterAdmission); err != nil {\n    objectMeta.SetManagedFields(managedFieldsBeforeAdmission)\n    warning.AddWarning(ctx, \"\", fmt.Sprintf(...))\n}\n```\n\n### 2.8 `ScaleHandler`\n\n**File:** `staging/src/k8s.io/apimachinery/pkg/util/managedfields/scalehandler.go`\n\nThe `scale` subresource presents a different object shape (`autoscaling/v1 Scale`) from its parent resource. `ScaleHandler` projects managed fields from the parent resource into the scale coordinate space (converting replica path locations and API versions), and projects updates back from scale to the parent. It uses `ResourcePathMappings` to declare the version-dependent field path for `spec.replicas`.\n\n---\n\n## 3. End-to-End Request Flow\n\nThe following describes what happens when a client sends:\n```\nPATCH /apis/apps/v1/namespaces/default/deployments/my-app\nContent-Type: application/apply-patch+yaml\nfieldManager: my-controller\n```\n\n### Step 1 — HTTP dispatch and validation\n\n`PatchResource` (handler factory) runs. It validates the content-type against the allowed patch types for the resource. For `ApplyYAMLPatchType`, `forceAllowCreate = true`, meaning the request may create the object if it does not exist.\n\n```go\n// staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/endpoints/handlers/patch.go:672-674\ncase types.ApplyYAMLPatchType:\n    p.mechanism = newApplyPatcher(p, scope.FieldManager, yaml.Unmarshal, yaml.UnmarshalStrict)\n    p.forceAllowCreate = true\n```\n\nThe patch body is read with `limitedReadBodyWithRecordMetric`, which enforces `MaxRequestBodyBytes` and records metrics.\n\n### Step 2 — Admission wrapper installation\n\nThe admission interface is wrapped with `NewManagedFieldsValidatingAdmissionController` before any admission calls are made. This ensures the guard is always in place regardless of which admission plugins are registered.\n\n### Step 3 — Transform chain assembly\n\nThree transformer functions are chained with `rest.DefaultUpdatedObjectInfo`:\n\n```go\n// staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/endpoints/handlers/patch.go:697\ntransformers := []rest.TransformFunc{p.applyPatch, p.applyAdmission, dedupOwnerReferencesTransformer}\n```\n\nThese transformers are called inside `GuaranteedUpdate` (the storage layer's optimistic concurrency primitive) once per retry cycle if a conflict occurs at the storage level.\n\n### Step 4 — `applyPatch` transformer (first call)\n\n`applyPatch` is invoked with the current live object from storage:\n- If the live object has no UID, the object does not exist, and `createNewObject` is called (the patch becomes a create).\n- If the object exists, `applyPatchToCurrentObject` is called.\n\nInside `applyPatchToCurrentObject`:\n\n1. The YAML body is parsed into `*unstructured.Unstructured`.\n2. `p.fieldManager.Apply(obj, patchObj, fieldManager, force)` is called.\n3. If `fieldValidation=Strict`, the body is re-parsed with the strict decoder to surface unknown fields as errors.\n\n### Step 5 — Manager chain traversal (Apply path)\n\n`fieldManager.Apply` (the public `FieldManager` facade) decodes existing `managedFields` from the live object, clears `managedFields` from the object, then calls through the decorator chain in order:\n\n```\nVersionCheckManager\n  → LastAppliedUpdater\n    → LastAppliedManager\n      → ProbabilisticSkipNonAppliedManager\n        → CapManagersManager\n          → BuildManagerInfoManager\n            → ManagedFieldsUpdater\n              → StripMetaManager\n                → structuredMergeManager  ← SMD merge happens here\n```\n\nEach layer has a specific concern (described in section 4). The SMD merge runs at the bottom.\n\n### Step 6 — SMD merge\n\n`structuredMergeManager.Apply`:\n\n1. Converts the live object to `typed.TypedValue` (using the OpenAPI-derived SMD schema). Duplicates are allowed here so that existing objects are not rejected for pre-existing anomalies.\n2. Converts the patch object to `typed.TypedValue`. Duplicates are *not* allowed — the applied configuration must be internally consistent.\n3. Calls `f.updater.Apply(liveObjTyped, patchObjTyped, apiVersion, managed.Fields(), manager, force)`.\n4. The SMD updater computes the new object by merging applied fields onto the live object, and computes updated `ManagedFields`. If there are conflicts and `force=false`, it returns `merge.Conflicts`.\n5. If a non-nil `newObjTyped` is returned, it is converted back to a Kubernetes object, defaults are applied, and the object is converted to the hub (internal) version.\n\n### Step 7 — `applyAdmission` transformer\n\nAfter the merge, mutating admission runs with the operation set to `Create` (if new) or `Update` (if existing). The admission guard wrapper validates managedFields after each webhook call.\n\n### Step 8 — Storage write\n\n`p.restPatcher.Update` (wrapping `registry.Store.Update`) calls `GuaranteedUpdate` on the storage backend. The storage layer performs an optimistic concurrency check using the object's `resourceVersion`. If another write happened between the read and the write, `GuaranteedUpdate` re-reads and retries the entire transformer chain from the top.\n\n### Step 9 — Object too large fallback\n\nIf the stored object exceeds the etcd value size limit (default 1.5 MiB), and the patch type is not SSA, the code retries once after dropping `managedFields`:\n\n```go\n// staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/endpoints/handlers/patch.go:713-723\nif isTooLargeError(err) && p.patchType != types.ApplyYAMLPatchType && p.patchType != types.ApplyCBORPatchType {\n    // retry without managedFields\n}\n```\n\nNotably this fallback does **not** apply to SSA requests — an SSA request that would cause an oversized object always fails.\n\n### Step 10 — Response\n\nThe stored object is returned to the client. On creation, HTTP 201; on update, HTTP 200.\n\n---\n\n## 4. The Manager Chain: Layered Decoration Pattern\n\n`NewDefaultFieldManager` constructs the chain as nested calls:\n\n```go\n// staging/src/k8s.io/apimachinery/pkg/util/managedfields/internal/fieldmanager.go:57-75\nreturn NewFieldManager(\n    NewVersionCheckManager(\n        NewLastAppliedUpdater(\n            NewLastAppliedManager(\n                NewProbabilisticSkipNonAppliedManager(\n                    NewCapManagersManager(\n                        NewBuildManagerInfoManager(\n                            NewManagedFieldsUpdater(\n                                NewStripMetaManager(f),\n                            ), kind.GroupVersion(), subresource,\n                        ), DefaultMaxUpdateManagers,\n                    ), objectCreater, DefaultTrackOnCreateProbability,\n                ), typeConverter, objectConverter, kind.GroupVersion(),\n            ),\n        ), kind,\n    ), subresource,\n)\n```\n\n### Layer responsibilities\n\n**`VersionCheckManager`** (`versioncheck.go`): For `Apply` only — validates that the GVK in the patch object matches the resource's expected GVK. Rejects mismatched versions with `400 Bad Request`. Has no effect on `Update`.\n\n**`LastAppliedUpdater`** (`lastappliedupdater.go`): For `Apply` only, and only when `manager == \"kubectl\"`. After a successful apply, if the object already has a `kubectl.kubernetes.io/last-applied-configuration` annotation, this layer rebuilds it to match the newly applied object. This keeps `kubectl apply` (client-side) and kubectl server-side apply in sync for objects that were previously managed by CSA.\n\n**`LastAppliedManager`** (`lastappliedmanager.go`): Handles the upgrade path from CSA to SSA. When `manager == \"kubectl\"` and an apply produces conflicts, this layer checks whether those conflicts are covered by the fields the CSA annotation previously owned. If so, it re-runs the apply with `force=true` for those fields, silently upgrading the object to SSA without requiring the operator to pass `--force-conflicts`.\n\n**`ProbabilisticSkipNonAppliedManager`** (`skipnonapplied.go`): On `Update`, if `managedFields` is currently empty (i.e., the object was never touched by SSA), it probabilistically decides whether to start tracking fields for this update. The default probability `DefaultTrackOnCreateProbability = 1` means tracking is always started at create time. For `Apply`, if `managedFields` is empty, it first runs an `Update` with `manager=\"before-first-apply\"` to attribute all pre-existing fields to a synthetic manager, preventing them from appearing as conflicts to the first applier.\n\n**`CapManagersManager`** (`capmanagers.go`): On `Update`, after fields are computed, checks whether the number of distinct update-type manager entries exceeds `DefaultMaxUpdateManagers = 10`. If so, it merges the oldest entries into versioned buckets named `\"ancient-changes\"`. This prevents unbounded growth of `managedFields` in objects touched by many different tools over time. Apply-type manager entries are not capped.\n\n**`BuildManagerInfoManager`** (`buildmanagerinfo.go`): Converts the plain manager string (e.g., `\"my-controller\"`) into a JSON-encoded `ManagedFieldsEntry` identifier that includes the operation type and API version. For apply entries, the APIVersion is excluded from the identifier so the same manager identity is stable across version changes. For update entries, APIVersion is included to distinguish `v1` updates from `v1beta1` updates by the same manager.\n\n**`ManagedFieldsUpdater`** (`managedfieldsupdater.go`): On `Update`, uses a placeholder manager `\"current-operation\"` to run the underlying merge, then detects whether any fields were actually taken. If so, it records the current UTC timestamp for the real manager and merges the new fields with any fields that manager already held. On `Apply`, it records the timestamp of a successful apply. If the apply produced no change (the patch is a no-op because all fields already match), `newObjTyped` is nil and the updater returns a deep copy of the live object without modifying timestamps.\n\n**`StripMetaManager`** (`stripmeta.go`): After any merge, removes certain metadata paths from the computed `managedFields` for the acting manager. The stripped paths are:\n- `apiVersion`, `kind`\n- `metadata.name`, `metadata.namespace`, `metadata.creationTimestamp`, `metadata.selfLink`, `metadata.uid`, `metadata.clusterName`, `metadata.generation`, `metadata.managedFields`, `metadata.resourceVersion`\n\nThese are system-controlled fields that should never appear in any manager's ownership set.\n\n---\n\n## 5. Conflict Detection and Handling\n\n### What counts as a conflict\n\nA conflict arises when the applied configuration includes a field that is already owned by a *different* manager. Ownership is tracked in `managedFields` as a `fieldpath.Set` — a compact encoding of field paths including list element keys.\n\nThe SMD `merge.Updater.Apply` returns `merge.Conflicts` when it finds such overlaps and `force=false`. The type is:\n\n```go\ntype Conflicts []Conflict\n\ntype Conflict struct {\n    Manager string\n    Path    fieldpath.Path\n}\n```\n\n### Converting conflicts to API errors\n\n`internal.NewConflictError` (`conflict.go`) converts `merge.Conflicts` into a `*errors.StatusError` with HTTP status 409 (`StatusConflict`). Each conflicting field becomes a `metav1.StatusCause` with type `CauseTypeFieldManagerConflict`:\n\n```go\n// staging/src/k8s.io/apimachinery/pkg/util/managedfields/internal/conflict.go:33-43\nfunc NewConflictError(conflicts merge.Conflicts) *errors.StatusError {\n    causes := []metav1.StatusCause{}\n    for _, conflict := range conflicts {\n        causes = append(causes, metav1.StatusCause{\n            Type:    metav1.CauseTypeFieldManagerConflict,\n            Message: fmt.Sprintf(\"conflict with %v\", printManager(conflict.Manager)),\n            Field:   conflict.Path.String(),\n        })\n    }\n    return errors.NewApplyConflict(causes, getConflictMessage(conflicts))\n}\n```\n\nThe conflict message includes the conflicting manager's name, its operation type, and — for update-type managers — the timestamp of the last update. This allows the operator to identify which process owns the field.\n\n### Resolving conflicts: force apply\n\nPassing `force=true` in `PatchOptions` (or `--force-conflicts` with kubectl) causes SMD to take ownership regardless. The previous manager's entry in `managedFields` loses those fields; if that empties the set, the manager entry is removed entirely.\n\n### The \"before-first-apply\" synthetic manager\n\nIf an object never had SSA applied to it, its `managedFields` is empty. When the first SSA request arrives, `ProbabilisticSkipNonAppliedManager.Apply` runs an update pass against an empty object using the real live object, attributing all existing fields to `\"before-first-apply\"`. This prevents the first applier from inheriting ownership of every pre-existing field unconditionally, but it also means the first apply will produce a conflict for any field the applier touches that was set by a non-SSA writer.\n\n---\n\n## 6. Client-Side Apply Compatibility Layer\n\nThe `LastAppliedManager` and `LastAppliedUpdater` layers together implement the migration path from `kubectl apply` (client-side) to SSA.\n\n### Upgrade path (`LastAppliedManager`)\n\nWhen `kubectl apply --server-side` is used for the first time on an object previously managed by client-side apply, the following sequence occurs:\n\n1. SSA apply is attempted normally.\n2. If conflicts are detected (against fields set by non-kubectl managers using `Update`), `LastAppliedManager` reads the `kubectl.kubernetes.io/last-applied-configuration` annotation from the live object.\n3. It computes the field set from the annotation and compares it against the live object using SMD's `Compare` method.\n4. Fields from the annotation that are *unchanged* in the live object (neither modified by others, nor added, nor removed) are treated as \"allowed conflicts\" — they were effectively owned by kubectl all along.\n5. If all conflicts fall within this allowed set, SSA is retried with `force=true` for those fields. If some conflicts lie outside the allowed set, the remaining conflicts are returned as a proper 409.\n\n```go\n// staging/src/k8s.io/apimachinery/pkg/util/managedfields/internal/lastappliedmanager.go:83-88\nif !conflictSet.Difference(allowedConflictSet).Empty() {\n    newConflicts := conflictsDifference(conflicts, allowedConflictSet)\n    return newLiveObj, newManaged, newConflicts\n}\nreturn f.fieldManager.Apply(liveObj, newObj, managed, manager, true)\n```\n\n### Annotation synchronization (`LastAppliedUpdater`)\n\nAfter a successful SSA apply by `kubectl`, `LastAppliedUpdater` reconstructs the `kubectl.kubernetes.io/last-applied-configuration` annotation from the applied object. This ensures that subsequent CSA operations (on clusters that may not support SSA, or on different objects) still find a coherent annotation.\n\n---\n\n## 7. Applyconfigurations: The Typed Client API\n\n### Purpose\n\nThe `applyconfigurations` package in `client-go` provides generated Go structs that are safe to use with SSA. These types differ from ordinary API types in a fundamental way: every field is a **pointer**, so the zero value of a field means \"absent from the applied configuration\" rather than \"explicitly set to zero\".\n\nA standard `appsv1.Deployment` has `Spec DeploymentSpec` (not a pointer). If you only want to set `Spec.Replicas`, you still must construct the entire `Spec` value. With the apply configuration type `appsv1apply.DeploymentApplyConfiguration`, every nested field is a pointer, so you only populate the fields you actually own.\n\n### Generated structure\n\n```go\n// staging/src/k8s.io/client-go/applyconfigurations/core/v1/pod.go:35-49\ntype PodApplyConfiguration struct {\n    metav1.TypeMetaApplyConfiguration    `json:\",inline\"`\n    *metav1.ObjectMetaApplyConfiguration `json:\"metadata,omitempty\"`\n    Spec   *PodSpecApplyConfiguration    `json:\"spec,omitempty\"`\n    Status *PodStatusApplyConfiguration  `json:\"status,omitempty\"`\n}\n```\n\nAll nested types follow the same pattern: optional pointer fields with `omitempty`. When marshaled to JSON/YAML, absent fields are omitted entirely, so the server only processes fields explicitly included in the apply payload.\n\n### Code generation\n\nStructs are generated by `applyconfiguration-gen`, part of `k8s.io/code-generator`:\n\n**Entry point:** `staging/src/k8s.io/code-generator/cmd/applyconfiguration-gen/main.go`\n**Generator core:** `staging/src/k8s.io/code-generator/cmd/applyconfiguration-gen/generators/applyconfiguration.go`\n\nThe generator inspects Go types (using `gengo`), follows JSON tags and type references, and emits a parallel type hierarchy under `client-go/applyconfigurations/<group>/<version>/`. For each root resource (a type tagged with `+k8s:deepcopy-gen:interfaces=k8s.io/apimachinery/pkg/runtime.Object`), it also generates:\n\n- A constructor (`func Pod(name, namespace string) *PodApplyConfiguration`) that pre-populates `Kind` and `APIVersion`.\n- A builder method for each field (`func (b *PodApplyConfiguration) WithSpec(value *PodSpecApplyConfiguration) *PodApplyConfiguration`).\n- An `ExtractPodFrom` function (if an OpenAPI type can be resolved), enabling the extract-modify-apply workflow.\n\n### Internal schema registry\n\n**File:** `staging/src/k8s.io/client-go/applyconfigurations/internal/internal.go`\n\nA single `Parser()` function returns a `*typed.Parser` that holds the full OpenAPI-derived SMD schema for all built-in types. This is used by `ExtractInto` to reconstruct an apply configuration from a live object.\n\n### The `ForKind` utility\n\n**File:** `staging/src/k8s.io/client-go/applyconfigurations/utils.go`\n\n`ForKind(gvk schema.GroupVersionKind)` returns a blank apply configuration struct for any registered kind. This is used internally by the generic SSA helpers in `client-go` to construct the target type without knowing the concrete type at compile time.\n\n### Extract-Modify-Apply workflow\n\n`ExtractInto` (`staging/src/k8s.io/apimachinery/pkg/util/managedfields/extract.go`) provides the read side of the workflow:\n\n1. Look up the manager's `ManagedFieldsEntry` with `Operation=Apply` in the live object.\n2. Decode `FieldsV1` into a `fieldpath.Set`.\n3. Call `typedObj.ExtractItems(fieldset.Leaves())` to get only the leaf values that the manager owns.\n4. Unmarshal the resulting unstructured map into the apply configuration type.\n\nThis means the extracted apply configuration contains exactly what the server recorded as owned by that manager — no more, no less. Modifying this and reapplying is safe and idempotent.\n\n```go\n// staging/src/k8s.io/apimachinery/pkg/util/managedfields/extract.go:53-88\nfunc ExtractInto(object runtime.Object, objectType typed.ParseableType, fieldManager string, applyConfiguration interface{}, subresource string) error {\n    typedObj, err := toTyped(object, objectType)\n    // ...\n    u := typedObj.ExtractItems(fieldset.Leaves()).AsValue().Unstructured()\n    // ...\n    return runtime.DefaultUnstructuredConverter.FromUnstructured(m, applyConfiguration)\n}\n```\n\nThe individual type-specific extract functions (e.g., `ExtractPodFrom`) are generated and simply call `ExtractInto` with the appropriate `ParseableType` from the internal schema registry:\n\n```go\n// staging/src/k8s.io/client-go/applyconfigurations/core/v1/pod.go:71\nerr := managedfields.ExtractInto(pod, internal.Parser().Type(\"io.k8s.api.core.v1.Pod\"), fieldManager, b, subresource)\n```\n\n---\n\n## 8. Extension Points and Customization Hooks\n\n### 8.1 Custom `TypeConverter`\n\nThe `internal.TypeConverter` interface is:\n\n```go\ntype TypeConverter interface {\n    ObjectToTyped(runtime.Object, ...typed.ValidationOptions) (*typed.TypedValue, error)\n    TypedToObject(*typed.TypedValue) (runtime.Object, error)\n}\n```\n\nAny code constructing a `FieldManager` can supply a custom implementation. The two built-in implementations are `typeConverter` (OpenAPI-backed) and `deducedTypeConverter` (CRD fallback). A custom converter could add domain-specific field coercion or logging.\n\n**Risk:** A custom converter that changes field identity (e.g., normalizing values during conversion) can cause spurious conflicts or silently drop fields from ownership sets.\n\n### 8.2 `resetFields` filter\n\nBoth `NewDefaultFieldManager` and `NewDefaultCRDFieldManager` accept a `resetFields map[fieldpath.APIVersion]fieldpath.Filter`. This is passed as `IgnoreFilter` to the SMD `merge.Updater`. Fields matching the filter are excluded from managed field tracking — they are always reset to the server's value regardless of what any manager sets.\n\nThis is used for fields like `status` in resources where status is managed exclusively by the system, not by any applier. The filter is per-APIVersion, allowing different versions to have different reset semantics.\n\n**Risk:** Incorrectly configured `resetFields` can silently discard user intent for the specified fields.\n\n### 8.3 Custom `Manager` chain wrappers\n\nAny code that calls `internal.NewFieldManager(f Manager, subresource string)` can supply an arbitrary `Manager` implementation as `f`. The built-in chain can be extended by wrapping `NewDefaultFieldManager`'s output with additional `Manager` decorators. However, there is no public registration API; extension requires calling the internal constructors directly.\n\n### 8.4 Admission controllers and `managedFields`\n\nMutating admission webhooks can technically modify `metadata.managedFields` on the object they receive. The `NewManagedFieldsValidatingAdmissionController` wrapper catches invalid resulting states and rolls back, but it cannot prevent semantically incorrect but structurally valid modifications. An admission webhook that adds or removes entries from `managedFields` will alter field ownership in ways that may be invisible to operators.\n\n### 8.5 `ScaleHandler` path mapping\n\n`ScaleHandler` uses `ResourcePathMappings` (a `map[string]fieldpath.Path`) to project replica-related fields between the main resource and the scale subresource. Resources that do not fit the standard `spec.replicas` path (e.g., custom replica semantics) can supply their own mapping when constructing the handler.\n\n---\n\n## 9. Operational Implications\n\n### 9.1 `managedFields` size growth\n\nEvery actor that writes to an object adds or updates an entry in `managedFields`. The stored representation (`FieldsV1`) is a compact JSON-encoded trie, but objects with many managers, many fields, and many API versions can accumulate hundreds of kilobytes in `managedFields` alone.\n\nThe `CapManagersManager` mitigates this for update-type managers by capping at 10 entries and merging older entries into `\"ancient-changes\"` buckets. Apply-type managers are not capped, and a resource with many independent appliers can grow its `managedFields` unboundedly.\n\n**Mitigation:** The `managedFields` on a stored object can be reset by sending a PATCH or PUT with an explicit empty `managedFields` list (`[]` in JSON, not `null`). The `isResetManagedFields` function in `fieldmanager.go` detects this:\n\n```go\n// staging/src/k8s.io/apimachinery/pkg/util/managedfields/internal/fieldmanager.go:169-178\nfunc isResetManagedFields(managedFields []metav1.ManagedFieldsEntry) bool {\n    if len(managedFields) == 0 {\n        return managedFields != nil\n    }\n    ...\n}\n```\n\nIf the list is explicitly set (even if empty), existing managedFields are discarded. Subsequent operations rebuild tracking from scratch.\n\n### 9.2 The `UpdateNoErrors` degraded mode\n\n`UpdateNoErrors` silently clears `managedFields` on the updated object if the underlying `Update` call fails:\n\n```go\n// staging/src/k8s.io/apimachinery/pkg/util/managedfields/internal/fieldmanager.go:145-163\nfunc (f *FieldManager) UpdateNoErrors(liveObj, newObj runtime.Object, manager string) runtime.Object {\n    obj, err := f.Update(liveObj, newObj, manager)\n    if err != nil {\n        // logs at most once per second\n        klog.ErrorS(err, \"[SHOULD NOT HAPPEN] failed to update managedFields\", ...)\n        RemoveObjectManagedFields(newObj)\n        return newObj\n    }\n    return obj\n}\n```\n\nThis is used by `jsonPatcher` and `smpPatcher` (non-SSA patches) where managedFields tracking is best-effort. If the OpenAPI schema is inconsistent or the type converter is misconfigured, tracking silently degrades. The error is logged at most once per second (`atMostEverySecond.Do(...)`) using `NewAtMostEvery`.\n\n### 9.3 GuaranteedUpdate and the retry loop\n\nBecause SSA is implemented as a transformer in `GuaranteedUpdate`'s retry loop, the entire merge — including SMD computation and admission — can run multiple times per request if other writers concurrently update the same object. This is expected and correct, but has performance implications for highly contended objects.\n\nEach retry re-reads the live object from etcd, re-runs the SMD merge, and re-runs admission. For resources with large schemas or many managed fields, each merge pass is CPU-bound (schema traversal, field set operations). Objects with hundreds of fields and an OpenAPI schema can take multiple milliseconds per merge pass.\n\n### 9.4 Schema-dependent performance\n\nThe `TypeConverter.ObjectToTyped` call validates the object against the SMD schema. For built-in types, the schema is compiled at startup and lookups are O(1) per GVK. For CRDs with `deducedTypeConverter`, the schema is structural but untyped, so merge operates without type coercion and is generally faster.\n\nStoring the full `GvkParser` (which covers all registered GVKs) in memory is intentional. At startup, `NewTypeConverter` processes the entire OpenAPI schema map — this is a fixed one-time cost.\n\n### 9.5 Subresource apply interactions\n\nSSA applied to a subresource only affects the fields within that subresource's schema. For `status`, the apply patch must not include ownership of fields outside `status`. For `scale`, the `ScaleHandler` translates ownership between coordinate spaces. Incorrectly applying to a subresource that shares field paths with the root resource (but with different semantics) can produce confusing ownership state, because the `ManagedFieldsEntry.Subresource` field is used to namespace ownership per subresource.\n\n### 9.6 CRD schema evolution\n\nWhen a CRD's OpenAPI schema changes (e.g., a field is renamed or moved), the SMD schema used by `TypeConverter` becomes inconsistent with stored `managedFields`. The stored `FieldsV1` paths may reference fields that no longer exist in the schema. SSA is tolerant of this for reads (fields not in the schema are simply not in the typed representation), but a subsequent apply will not include the stale paths in the new managed set, effectively abandoning them. This is a permanent, silent migration effect.\n\n---\n\n## 10. Failure Modes and Design Tradeoffs\n\n### 10.1 No schema, no granular ownership\n\nIf a GVK has no entry in the `TypeConverter`'s parser map (e.g., the type is not in the OpenAPI spec), `ObjectToTyped` returns `NoCorrespondingTypeError`. The fallback for CRDs is `deducedTypeConverter`, which uses SMD's type deduction — all list items are treated as atomic, meaning lists can only be replaced entirely, not merged by key. Custom resources with list fields benefit from structural schemas that declare `x-kubernetes-list-type: map` with `x-kubernetes-list-map-keys` to get granular list element ownership.\n\n### 10.2 Force-apply irreversibility\n\nWhen `force=true`, the displacing manager takes ownership. The previous owner is not notified. If a controller re-applies its configuration periodically (as is standard), it will eventually reclaim its fields and overwrite the force-applier's values. Force apply is thus a transient override, not a permanent one — unless the force-applier continues to maintain the field.\n\n### 10.3 Admission mutation and apply state divergence\n\nMutating webhooks can change fields in the applied object before it is persisted. Those changed fields are attributed to the manager that triggered the apply, even though the values came from a webhook. If the webhook changes a field the applier did not include in its configuration, that field is now in the applier's ownership set but not in the applier's intended state. On the next apply cycle, the applier's configuration may drop the field (because it was not explicitly included), removing the webhook's addition.\n\nThe guidance is that admission webhooks should not add entirely new fields to SSA-managed objects without being registered as their own field manager.\n\n### 10.4 Object-too-large: SSA never retries without managedFields\n\nNon-SSA patches have a fallback where managedFields are stripped if the object exceeds etcd's value size. SSA does not have this fallback because stripping `managedFields` from an SSA-applied object would permanently lose ownership state, making future applies unable to detect stale fields. The design choice is to fail hard rather than silently corrupt state.\n\n### 10.5 `managedFields` as a reliability signal\n\nThe `[SHOULD NOT HAPPEN]` log in `UpdateNoErrors` is rate-limited and signals schema/converter inconsistency. In practice, if this appears in cluster logs, it usually means an API server was rolled out with an incompatible OpenAPI schema change, or a custom type converter was provided with incorrect logic.\n\n---\n\n## 11. File and Directory Map\n\nThe following files were directly analyzed to produce this document.\n\n| Path | Role |\n|---|---|\n| `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/endpoints/handlers/patch.go` | HTTP handler for PATCH;
